Partial Choice Between Fidaa and Daf': The Three Scenarios and the Principle
Summarizing three partial-choice scenarios and the principle of disabling dispositions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios of partial choice between fidaa and daf', apply the principle that only actions disabling handover bind the master to fidaa, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding intercourse with a female slave.

Core Idea
Only a master's action that disables handover (daf') makes him bound to fidaa; intercourse does not.

This passage from al-Dhakhirah and al-Asl presents three crucial scenarios where a master makes a partial choice between paying ransom (fidaa) and handing over the slave (daf') after a jinaayah. These cases reveal a core Hanafi principle: the master's liability depends on whether his actions physically prevent the handover of the slave. Understanding these scenarios and the underlying principle will help you grasp the nuances of slave liability in Hanafi fiqh and the intra-school disagreement on what constitutes ikhtiyaar.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the core principle
The master becomes bound to fidaa only if he initiates a disposition (tasarruf) that disables him from handing over the slave, and he was aware of the crime at that time. Dispositions that do not disable handover (like intercourse) do not bind him.
This principle is the key to all three scenarios.
2
Scenario one: one victim, one heir
When there is a single victim and a single heir, the master's partial choice (e.g., fidaa for half) is treated as a choice for the entire slave, by agreement of all riwayaat.
The choice for half implies choice for the whole because the obligation is indivisible.
3
Scenario two: two victims, each with one heir
When there are two victims, each with one heir, the master's choice for one does not affect the other; he remains free to choose for the second. This is also agreed upon.
Each claim is independent.
4
Scenario three: one victim, two heirs
When there is one victim but two heirs, there is disagreement: most riwayaat say choosing fidaa for one binds him to fidaa for the other, but Kitab al-Durar says it does not.
The conflict arises from whether the partial choice implies the whole.
5
Apply the principle to specific dispositions
Emancipation disables handover and thus binds the master to fidaa. Intercourse does not disable handover (the slave can still be handed over), so according to the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) it does not bind; Zufar disagrees. Marriage and intercourse leading to pregnancy have variations.
This is the intra-Hanafi dispute highlighted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الذخيرة وفي الأصل: إذا جنى جناية وخير المولى بين الدفع والفداء فاختار نصف العبد واختار الفداء في نصفه الآخر فهذه المسألة على وجوه أحدها أن يكون ولي الجناية واحداً بأن قتل العبد رجلاً خطأ وله ولد واحد والقتل خطأ، وفي هذا الوجه إذا اختار المولى الفداء في نصف العبد يصير مختاراً للفداء في الكل لذلك، وإذا اختار نصف العبد يصير مختاراً لدفع الكل وهذا باتفاق الروايات . والثاني أن يكون المقتول اثنين بأن قتل العبد رجلين خطأ ولكل واحد منهما ابن واختار المولى الفداء في أحدهما أو الدفع فإنه يبقى على اختياره في حق الآخر وهذا باتفاق الروايات أيضاً. الثالث إذا كان المقتول واحداً وله وليان فاختار المولى الفداء في حق الآخر ففي عامة الروايات يكون مختاراً للفداء، وفي كتاب الدرر لا يكون مختاراً للفداء، والأصل في هذه المسألة أن المولى متى أحدث في العبد تصرفاً . يعجزه عن الدفع وهو غير عالم بالجناية يصير مختاراً، وإذا أحدث تصرفاً لا يعجزه عن الدفع لا يصير مختاراً. وإن كان عالماً بالجناية، فإذا ثبت هذا الأصل فنقول الإعتاق تصرف يعجزه عن الدفع لأن إعتاقه نافذ وبعد العتق لا يمكنه الدفع فإذا أعتق مع العلم بالجناية يكون مختاراً للفداء، ولو كانت أمة فوطئها فهذا ليس باختيار للفداء عند علمائنا الثلاثة. وقال زفر رحمه الله : يكون مختاراً للفداء وكذلك إذا تزوجها لا يكون مختاراً للفداء. وفي الظهيرية إلا إذا أحبلها وفي التهذيب : ولو كانت أمة فتزوجها مختاراً للفداء، وكذلك إذا وطئها لا يكون مختاراً للفداء إلا إذا كانت بكراً أو علقت . لا يصير
And in al-Dhakhirah and al-Asl: If he commits an offense and the master is given the choice between handover and ransom, and he chooses half of the slave and chooses ransom for the other half, then this issue has aspects: First, that the guardian of the offense is one, as when the slave kills a man by mistake and he has one son, and the killing is mistake. In this aspect, if the master chooses ransom for half the slave, he becomes chooser of ransom for the entire slave for that reason; and if he chooses half the slave, he becomes chooser of handover for the entire slave, and this is by agreement of the riwayaat. Second, that the slain are two, as when the slave kills two men by mistake and each has a son, and the master chooses ransom for one or handover; then he remains on his choice with respect to the other, and this is also by agreement of the riwayaat. Third, when the slain is one and he has two guardians, and the master chooses ransom with respect to the other, then in the general riwayaat he becomes a chooser of ransom, but in the book al-Durar he does not become a chooser of ransom. And the principle in this issue is that whenever the master initiates a disposition in the slave that disables him from handover, while he is unaware of the offense, he becomes a chooser; and if he initiates a disposition that does not disable him from handover, he does not become a chooser. And if he is aware of the offense, then when this principle is established, we say: emancipation is a disposition that disables him from handover, because his emancipation is effective and after emancipation he cannot hand over; so if he emancipates while aware of the offense, he becomes a chooser of ransom. And if she is a female slave and he has intercourse with her, this is not a choice for ransom according to our three imams. And Zufar, may Allah have mercy on him, said: he becomes a chooser of ransom. And likewise, if he marries her, he does not become a chooser of ransom. And in al-Zahirah, except if he impregnates her. And in al-Tahdhib: if she is a female slave and he marries her, he becomes a chooser of ransom; and likewise if he has intercourse with her, he does not become a chooser of ransom unless she was a virgin or becomes pregnant. He does not become.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage from al-Dhakhirah and al-Asl summarizes three scenarios when the master makes a partial choice between fidaa and daf'. The guiding principle is whether the master's action disables the possibility of handing over the slave (daf'). Three cases are presented: (1) One victim, one heir: choosing fidaa for half makes him bound to fidaa for the whole; choosing daf' for half makes him bound to daf' for the whole. This is agreed upon. (2) Two victims, each with one heir: choosing fidaa for one or daf' for one leaves his choice open for the other. Also agreed. (3) One victim, two heirs: choosing fidaa for one heir makes him bound to fidaa for the other according to most riwayaat, but in Kitab al-Durar he does not become bound. The principle: any disposition that prevents handover (like emancipation) makes the master bound to fidaa if he knew of the offense. But intercourse with a female slave does not bind him according to the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), though Zufar disagrees. Similarly, marriage does not bind. However, al-Zahirah and al-Tahdhib have exceptions for intercourse leading to pregnancy or virginity. This shows the nuanced ikhtilaaf within the Hanafi school on what constitutes ikhtiyaar for fidaa.

Key Terms
تصرف (tasarruf): A legal disposition by the master affecting the slave, such as sale, emancipation, or marriage.
فداء (fidaa): Ransom payment made by the master to the victim's guardians to retain the slave.
دفع (daf'): Handing over the slave to the victim's guardians in lieu of ransom.
اختيار (ikhtiyaar): The master's binding choice between fidaa and daf'; certain actions make him effectively choose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), does a master who has intercourse with a female slave who committed jinaayah become bound to fidaa?
A) Yes, in all cases
B) No, never
C) Yes, only if she becomes pregnant
D) No, but only if the master was unaware of the crime

Key Takeaway
Only a master's action that disables handover (daf') binds him to fidaa; ordinary actions like intercourse do not, though later texts carve exceptions for pregnancy.

Master's Options When a Slave Kills a Fellow Slave
Ruling on master's choice when slave kills fellow slave or is injured by outsider

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the master's two options when his slave kills another slave and identify the scenarios where these options apply.

Core Idea
When a slave kills a fellow slave, the master chooses: hand over the killer or ransom him with the slain slave's value.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq introduces the master's rights and duties when his slave commits a crime against another slave belonging to the same master. The ruling grants the master a choice, balancing the victim's heirs' right to retribution with the master's property interest. Understanding this option is crucial for correctly handling such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is a slave killing another slave belonging to the same master. The ruling is that the master is given a choice between two options: hand over the killer slave (daf') or pay the value of the slain slave as ransom (fida').
The choice is a right of the master, not a strict obligation.
2
Examine the options
Option 1 (daf'): the master hands over the killer slave to the victim's heirs, freeing himself from liability. Option 2 (fida'): the master keeps his slave but must pay the value of the slain slave.
The value is assessed at the time of killing.
3
Consider the injury by a foreigner scenario
If a foreign slave injures the master's slave (e.g., cuts off a hand), the foreign slave is given the choice between paying compensation (arsh) or being handed over for retaliation. Then the master of the injured slave may also be asked to hand over his slave or ransom him.
This extends the principle of choice to multiple parties.
4
Note the exception for intentional killing
The rule about liability upon freeing the slave applies only to accidental killing (khata'). If the killing was intentional and the master frees the slave, nothing is owed by the master, as liability shifts to the slave.
This distinction affects the master's potential liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب جناية المملوك والجناية عليه ولو لم يقتله عبد الأجنبي ولكنه قتله عبد آخر لمولاه فإنه يخير المولى بين الدفع والفداء بقيمة العبد المقتول فإن دفعه العبد إليه سلم لهم، وإن اختار الفداء يفدى بقيمة العبد المقتول. ولو قطع الأجنبي يد هذا وفقأ عينه أو جراحة فيخير العبد الأجنبي، فإن دفع أو فداه بالأرش فإنه يقال لمولى العبد المفقوءة عينه ادفع عبدك هذا إلى ولي الجناية أو افده، وقيد الضمان في العتق يكون للقتل خطأ لأنه لو كان عمداً فأعتق لا يلزمه شيء
Chapter of the Injury of the Slave and Injury against Him. And if a slave was not killed by a foreign slave, but rather he was killed by another slave belonging to the same master, then the master is given the choice between handing over [the killer slave] and ransoming him with the value of the slain slave. If he hands the slave over to them, they are done. And if he chooses ransom, he ransoms with the value of the slain slave. And if a foreigner cuts off the hand of this [slave] and gouges out his eye, or inflicts a wound, then the foreign slave is given the choice; if he hands over or ransoms with the compensation, then it is said to the master of the slave whose eye was gouged: 'Hand over this slave of yours to the guardian of the injury or ransom him.' And the restriction of liability in [the case of] freeing is for accidental killing because if it were intentional and he freed, nothing would be incumbent upon him.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on injuries involving slaves. The ruling states: if a slave kills another slave belonging to the same master, the master has an option (takhyir) between two courses: (1) he may hand over the offending slave (daf') to the heirs of the slain slave, in which case the master is free of any further liability, or (2) he may pay the value (qimah) of the slain slave as ransom (fida') and keep his slave. The value is assessed at the time of the killing. The passage then addresses a scenario where a foreign outsider (i.e., not the slave's master) injures the slave—by cutting off his hand, gouging out an eye, or wounding. In that case, the foreign slave (the perpetrator) is given the choice between paying the compensation (arsh) and being handed over for retaliation. If he chooses one, the master of the injured slave is then told to either hand over his slave (for retribution against the injury) or ransom him. The final sentence notes that the rule regarding guarantee (daman) upon freeing the slave applies only to accidental killing (khata'); if the slave killed intentionally, and the master frees him, nothing is owed by the master. This is because in intentional killing, the liability shifts to the slave himself.

Key Terms
جناية (jināya): A criminal act causing harm to a person, such as killing, wounding, or cutting off a limb.
دفع (daf'): The act of handing over the offending slave to the victim's heirs, freeing the master from liability.
فداء (fidā'): The payment of the slave's value (qimah) as ransom to keep the slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a slave kills another slave belonging to the same master, what options does the master have?
A) He must hand over the slave.
B) He may choose between handing over the slave or paying his value.
C) He must pay the full diyah.
D) He must free the slave.

Key Takeaway
The master of a slave who kills a fellow slave has the right to choose between handing over the killer or paying the slain slave's value as ransom.

Intentional Killing by Slave: Master's Liability and Pardon by One Heir
Rulings on intentional killing by a slave and pardon by one heir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the liability of a master when a slave commits intentional murder and is freed, and the effect of pardon by one heir on the remaining heir's claim.

Core Idea
The slave is personally liable for qisas and its monetary conversion; freeing him does not transfer liability to the master.

This lesson examines two interrelated rulings from the Hanafi school regarding a slave who commits intentional murder. First, if the master frees the slave after the killing, the master bears no liability. Second, if the victim has multiple heirs and only some pardon, the pardoning voids their right to qisas, and the share of the remaining heirs converts to a monetary claim that the slave must satisfy through istis'a' (compulsory labour). These rulings illustrate the Hanafi principle that the slave's personal responsibility for intentional crimes is not affected by the master's actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Read the first ruling: a slave kills a man intentionally; retaliation (qisas) becomes obligatory. The master frees the slave. The ruling: nothing is incumbent upon the master.
This is a clear statement of non-liability.
2
Determine the reason for master's non-liability
The slave's liability for intentional killing is personal (thabatat fi dhimmatihi). Freeing the slave does not transfer that liability to the master because the obligation is on the slave's person, not on the master's property.
This contrasts with unintentional killing, where the 'aqlah or master may be liable.
3
Identify the effect of pardon by one heir
The second ruling: if the victim has two sons and one pardons, the pardon voids that heir's right to retaliation. The other heir's share (one-half) becomes a monetary claim (mal).
The pardon does not affect the other heir's right; it merely converts its nature.
4
Explain the mechanism for the remaining heir
The remaining heir may compel the slave to work (istis'a') to earn half his value. The master is not required to pay half the value.
Istis'a' allows the slave to pay off the debt through labour.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold the master liable for the slave's value if he frees him after the crime, arguing that freeing deprives the heirs of the slave's value. The Hanafi position is that the slave remains personally liable, and the heirs can claim from him via istis'a'.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate and based on different usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كان العبد قتل رجلاً عمداً ووجب القصاص فأعتقه مولاه فلا يلزم المولى شيء، ولو كان للمقتول ولدان فعفا أحدهما بطل حقه وانقلب نصيب الآخر مالاً فله أن يستسعى العبد في نصف قيمته ولا يجب على المولى نصف القيمة.
And if the slave killed a man intentionally and retaliation became obligatory, and his master freed him, then nothing is incumbent upon the master. And if the slain had two sons, and one of them pardoned, his right became void, and the share of the other turned into monetary compensation; so he may compel the slave to work for half his value, and half the value is not obligatory upon the master.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage provides two rulings. First: if a slave commits intentional murder (qatl 'amd), retaliation (qisas) becomes obligatory on the slave. If the master frees the slave after the killing, the master is not liable for anything—neither the slave's value nor the diyah—because the liability for intentional killing falls on the slave personally, and freeing him does not transfer that liability to the master. Second: if the victim has two sons (heirs), and one of them pardons the slave (i.e., forgives the qisas), then the pardon voids the right of that heir to retaliation. The other heir's share (the right to qisas) is converted into a monetary claim (mal); he is entitled to half the slave's value. He can compel the slave to work (istis'a') to pay off this amount. The master is not required to pay half the value; the obligation is on the slave.

Key Terms
قصاص (qiṣāṣ): Retaliation in kind for intentional killing or injury.
استسعاء (istis'ā'): Compelling a slave to work to earn money to pay a debt.
عمد (ʿamd): Intentional act, here referring to intentional killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a slave kills a man intentionally and one of the victim's two sons pardons the slave, what happens?
A) The slave is freed.
B) The master must pay half the slave's value.
C) The other son can compel the slave to work for half his value.
D) The entire matter is dropped.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a slave's personal liability for intentional murder remains even if freed, and the pardon by one heir converts the remaining heirs' share into a monetary claim enforceable through istis'a'.
